## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the fundamental problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from simple exponential/logistic growth to more complex forms involving Allee effects, Gompertz growth, and time-dependent parameters.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth common in tumor/population models)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * P * (1 - c1 * P) (quadratic dependence at low density)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent with hyperbolic saturation)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * t) (logistic with time-dependent growth rate)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * sin(c2 * t + c3) (periodic environmental forcing)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Time-decaying growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Ratio-dependent: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * P * t (linear time trend in growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence on P (dP/dt ∝ P) indicates density-independent exponential growth regime
- Quadratic term in P (dP/dt contains P² term with negative coefficient) indicates logistic-type density-dependent regulation
- Cubic terms in P suggest Allee effects or bistability in population dynamics
- Logarithmic dependence on P (log(P) terms) suggests Gompertz-type growth with multiplicative stochastic origins
- Product of P with trigonometric function of t indicates seasonal or periodic environmental forcing
- Ratio P/(c+P) structure indicates resource-limited growth with Michaelis-Menten-type saturation kinetics
- Growth rate that changes sign at specific P values indicates equilibrium points (carrying capacity or extinction threshold)
- Fractional powers of P (P^c where 0<c<1) suggest surface-area-to-volume scaling in organism growth
- Time appearing only in multiplicative combination with P-dependent terms suggests slowly varying environmental parameters
- Multiple roots in dP/dt as a function of P indicate multiple equilibria and potential regime shifts
